| S-001 | security | Returns raw `(e as Error).message` (network/socket error text) to the client. SocksProxyAgent / HttpsProxyAgent errors built from `buildProxyUrl(config)` may surface the proxy URL — credentials are URL-encoded inside it. | `src/app/api/proxy/test/route.ts:70-71` | — | Authorised localhost / admin-token caller, but the response is rendered into the Settings UI and a forwarded log could leak the proxy host or even auth fragments if the underlying agent ever stringifies the URL in its error message. | VERIFIED_WITH_SOURCE: proxy/test/route.ts:139 (error wrapped in sanitizeUnknownError before JSON response) |
| S-004 | security | GET returns `error: \`Steam sync failed: ${safe}\`` containing the raw masked error message. | SRC-API-001 | api | The `cleanup()` function sets `aborted = true` but the `cancel()` method (lines 74-76) can race with `req.signal.addEventListener('abort', cleanup)` (line 69). If the stream consumer cancels without triggering the abort signal, there's no guaranteed cleanup sequence. Additionally, `controller.enqueue()` can silently fail if the controller is already closed (line 43), but the code depends on the `aborted` flag catching this. However, if an exception is thrown *inside* `controller.enqueue()` before the catch clause, the flag doesn't get set immediately. | `/api/download-status/stream/route.ts` (lines 38-87) | — | - Wrap cleanup calls with an idempotency guard | VERIFIED_WITH_SOURCE: download-status/stream/route.ts:57-67,74-76 |
| SRC-API-002 | api | The `PATCH` handler performs multiple `setAppSetting` calls (lines 255-577) before wrapping the activity log in a try-catch (lines 579-586). If the activity log fails, the settings were already persisted. This violates atomicity — the audit trail won't reflect what was changed, creating a compliance gap for credential updates (token, API key). | `/api/settings/route.ts` (lines 241-592) | — | - Batch all DB writes into a single transaction wrapper | DONE_WITH_DIFF: settings PATCH writes+audit wrapped in db.transaction (commit 13cfc85e) |
| SRC-API-003 | api | Both routes call `precheckContentLength()` but the request size limit is enforced *after* the multipart/form-data header check (line 34 in series image). A malformed multipart with a huge content-length could consume memory during `formData()` parsing (line 39) before being rejected. The precheck happens at line 37, but formData parsing is not wrapped. | `/api/producer/[id]/logo/route.ts` (line 31), `/api/series/[id]/image/route.ts` (line 37) | — | - Move `precheckContentLength()` to the very first check (before content-type validation) | VERIFIED_WITH_SOURCE: producer/[id]/logo/route.ts:18-19; series/[id]/image/route.ts:25-26 |
| SRC-API-004 | api | Routes validate VN IDs using `/^(v\d+\|egs_\d+)$/i` (case-insensitive flag). This allows `V123`, `V123`, `EGS_456` as inputs, but the codebase elsewhere uses lowercase (`v123`, `egs_456`) as the canonical form. This inconsistency could cause: | Multiple routes (e.g., `/api/vn/[id]/route.ts` line 20, `/api/vn/[id]/stock/route.ts` line 23) | — | - Normalize all VN IDs to lowercase immediately after validation: `id.toLowerCase()` | VERIFIED_WITH_SOURCE: vn/[id]/route.ts:17 + vn/[id]/stock/route.ts:23,32 (rawId.toLowerCase() before regex test) |

| SRC-API-006 | api | The `parseEgsId()` function (lines 29-35) strips `egs_` prefix, then converts to number. But a param like `egs_` (with nothing after underscore) becomes `""`, `Number("")` is 0, and the check `n <= 0` rejects it. However, a param like `egs_abc` becomes `Number("abc")` which is `NaN`, and `NaN <= 0` is `false`, so it's accepted as a valid ID. The route then calls `getEgsVnLink(egsId)` with `NaN`, which could cause unexpected behavior downstream. | `/api/egs/[id]/vndb/route.ts` lines 29-35 | — | - Use strict: `const n = Number(cleaned); if (!Number.isSafeInteger(n) \|\| n <= 0) return null;` | VERIFIED_WITH_SOURCE: egs/[id]/vndb/route.ts:30-35 (parseEgsId uses Number.isSafeInteger; egs_abc→NaN now rejected) |

| SRC-API-008 | api | Public GET routes (like `/api/collection/route.ts` line 42) rely on code comments to signal they're intentionally unauthed.
